src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Christian_science_church122908_02.jpg/220px-Christian_science_church122908_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christian_science_church122908_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Since late 2009, the headquarters of the Internet Archive has been the building that formerly housed the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Church_of_Christ,_Scientist_(San_Francisco,_California)" title="Fourth Church of Christ, Scientist (San Francisco, California)">Fourth Church of Christ, Scientist (San Francisco, California)</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Internet Archive</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Digital_library" title="Digital library">digital library</a> with the stated mission of "universal access to all knowledge".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;notes 2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;notes 3&#93;</a></sup> It provides free public access to collections of digitized materials, including websites, software applications/games, music, movies/videos, moving images, and millions of books. In addition to its archiving function, the Archive is an activist organization, advocating a free and open Internet. As of April 2021, the Internet Archive holds over 30 million books and texts, 8.9 million movies, videos and TV shows, 649,000 software programs, 13,225,000 audio files, 3.8 million images, and 552 billion web pages in the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.\n</p><p>The Internet Archive allows the public to upload and download digital material to its data cluster, but the bulk of its data is collected automatically by its web crawlers, which work to preserve as much of the public web as possible. Its web archive, the Wayback Machine, contains hundreds of billions of web captures.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;notes 4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The Archive also oversees one of the world\'s largest book digitization projects.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" security letters</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Opposition_to_SOPA_and_PIPA_bills"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Opposition to SOPA and PIPA bills</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Opposition_to_Google_Books_settlement"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Opposition to Google Books settlement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Nintendo_Power_magazine"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Nintendo Power</i> magazine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Government_of_India"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Government of India</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Turkey"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Turkey</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#National_Emergency_Library"><span class="tocnumber">7.8</span> <span class="toctext">National Emergency Library</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Publishers&#39;_lawsuit"><span class="tocnumber">7.9</span> <span class="toctext">Publishers\' lawsuit</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Ceramic_archivists_collection"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Ceramic archivists collection</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Artists_in_residence"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Artists in residence</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Similar_projects"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Similar projects</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2020</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg/220px-Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg/330px-Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg/440px-Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Internet_Archive_-_Bibliotheca_Alexandrina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mirror of the Internet Archive in the <a href="/wiki/Bibliotheca_Alexandrina" title="Bibliotheca Alexandrina">Bibliotheca Alexandrina</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Archive is a <a href="/wiki/501(c)(3)_organization" title="501(c)(3) organization">501(c)(3)</a> nonprofit operating in the United States. It has an annual budget of $10 million, derived from revenue from its Web crawling services, various partnerships, grants, donations, and the <a href="/wiki/Kahle-Austin_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Kahle-Austin Foundation">Kahle-Austin Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The Internet Archive also manages periodic funding campaigns. For instance, a December 2019 campaign had a goal of reaching $6 million in donations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Archive is headquartered in San Francisco, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. From 1996 to 2009, its headquarters were in the <a href="/wiki/Presidio_of_San_Francisco" title="Presidio of San Francisco">Presidio of San Francisco</a>, a former U.S. military base. Since 2009, its headquarters have been at 300 Funston Avenue in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Church_of_Christ,_Scientist_(San_Francisco,_California)" title="Fourth Church of Christ, Scientist (San Francisco, California)">Christian Science Church</a>.  At one time, most of its staff worked in its <a href="/wiki/Book_scanning" title="Book scanning">book-scanning</a> centers; as of 2019, scanning is performed by 100 paid operators worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  The Archive also has <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data centers</a> in three Californian cities: San Francisco, <a href="/wiki/Redwood_City,_California" title="Redwood City, California">Redwood City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_California" title="Richmond, California">Richmond</a>. To reduce the risk of data loss, the Archive creates copies of parts of its collection at more distant locations, including the <a href="/wiki/Bibliotheca_Alexandrina" title="Bibliotheca Alexandrina">Bibliotheca Alexandrina</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;notes 5&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and a facility in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Archive is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Internet_Preservation_Consortium" title="International Internet Preservation Consortium">International Internet Preservation Consortium</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and was officially designated as a library by the state of California in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;notes 6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg/220px-Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg/330px-Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg/440px-Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Internet_Archive_headquarters_exterior_February_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2008 headquarters</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Brewster_Kahle" title="Brewster Kahle">Brewster Kahle</a> founded the Archive in May 1996 around the same time that he began the for-profit web crawling company <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;notes 7&#93;</a></sup> In October 1996, the Internet Archive had begun to archive and preserve the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> in large quantities,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;notes 8&#93;</a></sup> though it saved the earliest pages in May 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The archived content wasn\'t available to the general public until 2001, when it developed the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.\n</p><p>In late 1999, the Archive expanded its collections beyond the Web archive, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Prelinger_Archives" title="Prelinger Archives">Prelinger Archives</a>. Now the Internet Archive includes texts, audio, moving images, and software. It hosts a number of other projects: the <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> Images Archive, the contract crawling service Archive-It, and the wiki-editable library catalog and book information site <a href="/wiki/Open_Library" title="Open Library">Open Library</a>. Soon after that, the Archive began working to provide specialized services relating to the <a href="/wiki/Information_access" title="Information access">information access</a> needs of the print-disabled; publicly accessible books were made available in a protected Digital Accessible Information System (DAISY) format.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;notes 9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to its website:<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;notes 10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Most societies place importance on preserving artifacts of their culture and heritage. Without such artifacts, civilization has no memory and no mechanism to learn from its successes and failures. Our culture now produces more and more artifacts in digital form. The Archive\'s mission is to help preserve those artifacts and create an Internet library for researchers, historians, and scholars.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In August 2012, the Archive announced<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> that it has added <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent" title="BitTorrent">BitTorrent</a> to its file download options for more than 1.3 million existing files, and all newly uploaded files.<sup id="cite_ref-TFBT_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TFBT-22">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This method is the fastest means of downloading media from the Archive, as files are served from two Archive data centers, in addition to other torrent clients which have downloaded and continue to serve the files.<sup id="cite_ref-TFBT_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TFBT-22">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;notes 11&#93;</a></sup> On November 6, 2013, the Internet Archive\'s headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Richmond_District,_San_Francisco" title="Richmond District, San Francisco">San Francisco\'s Richmond District</a> caught fire,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> destroying equipment and damaging some nearby apartments.<sup id="cite_ref-fire2013_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fire2013-26">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> According to the Archive, it lost a side-building housing one of 30 of its scanning centers; cameras, lights, and scanning equipment worth hundreds of thousands of dollars; and "maybe 20 boxes of books and film, some irreplaceable, most already digitized, and some replaceable".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The nonprofit Archive sought donations to cover the estimated $600,000 in damage.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2016, Kahle announced that the Internet Archive was building the Internet Archive of Canada, a copy of the Archive to be based somewhere in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The announcement received widespread coverage due to the implication that the decision to build a backup archive in a foreign country was because of the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">presidency of Donald Trump</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KahleCanada_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KahleCanada-29">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Kahle was quoted as saying:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>On November 9th in America, we woke up to a new administration promising radical change. It was a firm reminder that institutions like ours, built for the long-term, need to design for change. For us, it means keeping our cultural materials safe, private and perpetually accessible. It means preparing for a Web that may face greater restrictions. It means serving patrons in a world in which government surveillance is not going away; indeed it looks like it will increase. Throughout history, libraries have fought against terrible violations of privacy\xe2\x80\x94where people have been rounded up simply for what they read. At the Internet Archive, we are fighting to protect our readers\' privacy in the digital world.<sup id="cite_ref-KahleCanada_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KahleCanada-29">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Beginning in 2017, <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a> and the Internet Archive have collaborated to make the Archive\'s records of digitized books available in <a href="/wiki/WorldCat" title="WorldCat">WorldCat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2018, the Internet Archive visual arts residency, which is organized by Amir Saber Esfahani and Andrew McClintock, helps connect artists with the Archive\'s over 48 <a href="/wiki/Petabyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Petabyte">petabytes</a><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;notes 12&#93;</a></sup> of digitized materials. Over the course of the yearlong residency, visual artists create a body of work which culminates in an exhibition. The hope is to connect digital history with the arts and create something for future generations to appreciate online or off.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Previous artists in residence include <a href="/wiki/Taravat_Talepasand" title="Taravat Talepasand">Taravat Talepasand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Lynn" title="Whitney Lynn">Whitney Lynn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Odell" title="Jenny Odell">Jenny Odell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, its headquarters in San Francisco received a <a href="/wiki/Bomb_threat" title="Bomb threat">bomb threat</a> which forced a temporary evacuation of the building.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Internet Archive acquires most materials from donations,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;notes 13&#93;</a></sup> such as hundreds of thousands of 78&#160;rpm discs from <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Library" title="Boston Public Library">Boston Public Library</a> in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> a donation of 250,000 books from <a href="/wiki/Trent_University" title="Trent University">Trent University</a> in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and the entire collection of <a href="/wiki/Marygrove_College" title="Marygrove College">Marygrove College</a>\'s library in 2020 after it closed.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> All material is then digitized and retained in digital storage, while a digital copy is returned to the original holder and the Internet Archive\'s copy, if not in the public domain, is borrowed to patrons worldwide one at a time under the <a href="/wiki/Controlled_digital_lending" title="Controlled digital lending">controlled digital lending</a> (CDL) theory of the <a href="/wiki/First-sale_doctrine" title="First-sale doctrine">first-sale doctrine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Web_archiving">Web archiving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Web archiving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wayback_Machine">Wayback Machine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Wayback Machine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg/220px-Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="59" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg/330px-Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg/440px-Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="546" data-file-height="147" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wayback_Machine_logo_2010.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wayback Machine logo, used since 2001</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin thumbimage" data-durationhint="869.51933333333" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Wikimania_2019_-_Mark_Graham_(ENG).mp3" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/56/Wikimania_2019_-_Mark_Graham_%28ENG%29.mp3/Wikimania_2019_-_Mark_Graham_%28ENG%29.mp3.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Ogg Vorbis" data-shorttitle="Ogg Vorbis" data-transcodekey="ogg" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="72160" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/56/Wikimania_2019_-_Mark_Graham_%28ENG%29.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="Original MP3 file (192 kbps)" data-shorttitle="MP3 source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="192000" /></audio></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimania_2019_-_Mark_Graham_(ENG).mp3" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mark Graham</div></div></div>\n<p>The Internet Archive capitalized on the popular use of the term "<a href="/wiki/WABAC_machine" class="mw-redirect" title="WABAC machine">WABAC Machine</a>" from a segment of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Rocky_and_Bullwinkle_and_Friends" title="The Adventures of Rocky and Bullwinkle and Friends">The Adventures of Rocky and Bullwinkle</a></i> cartoon (specifically, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Rocky_and_Bullwinkle_and_Friends#Supporting_features" title="The Adventures of Rocky and Bullwinkle and Friends">Peabody\'s Improbable History</a></i>), and uses the name "Wayback Machine" for its service that allows archives of the World Wide Web to be searched and accessed.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> This service allows users to view some of the archived web pages. The Wayback Machine was created as a joint effort between Alexa Internet (owned by <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a>) and the Internet Archive when a three-dimensional index was built to allow for the browsing of archived web content.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;notes 14&#93;</a></sup> Millions of web sites and their associated data (images, source code, documents, etc.) are saved in a database. The service can be used to see what previous versions of web sites used to look like, to grab original source code from web sites that may no longer be directly available, or to visit web sites that no longer even exist. Not all web sites are available because many web site owners choose to exclude their sites. As with all sites based on data from web crawlers, the Internet Archive misses large areas of the web for a variety of other reasons. A 2004 paper found international biases in the coverage, but deemed them "not intentional".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/220px-Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/330px-Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/440px-Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Incoming_additional_storage_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A purchase of additional storage at the Internet Archive</div></div></div>\n<p>A "Save Page Now" archiving feature was made available in October 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-savepage_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-savepage-45">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> accessible on the lower right of the Wayback Machine\'s main page.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;notes 15&#93;</a></sup> Once a target URL is entered and saved, the web page will become part of the Wayback Machine.<sup id="cite_ref-savepage_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-savepage-45">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\nThrough the Internet address web.archive.org,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> users can upload to the Wayback Machine a large variety of contents, including <a href="/wiki/PDF" title="PDF">PDF</a> and <a href="/wiki/Data_compression" title="Data compression">data compression</a> file formats. The Wayback Machine creates a permanent local URL of the upload content, that is accessible in the web, even if not listed while searching in the http://archive.org official website.\n</p><p>May 12, 1996, is the date of the oldest archived pages on the archive.org WayBack Machine, such as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/19960512212113/http://www.infoseek.com///">infoseek.com</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2016, it was announced that the way web pages are counted would be changed, resulting in the decrease of the archived pages counts shown.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th>Archived pages (billions)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2005\n</td>\n<td>40<sup 27&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2018\n</td>\n<td>344<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;notes 28&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_old_counting_systemA"><a href="#ref_old_counting_systemA"><b><sup>A</sup></b></a></span>  Using the old counting system used before October 2016<br />\n<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_new_counting_systemB"><a href="#ref_new_counting_systemB"><b><sup>B</sup></b></a></span>  Using the new counting system used after October 2016\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table><p>\nIn September 2020, the Internet Archive announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Cloudflare" title="Cloudflare">Cloudflare</a> to automatically index websites served via its "Always Online" services.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archive-It">Archive-It<span class="anchor" id="Archive-It"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Archive-It">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_1" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/Internet-archive-brewster-kahle-2013-0329.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Internet-archive-brewster-kahle-2013-0329.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brewster_Kahle" title="Brewster Kahle">Brewster Kahle</a> of the Internet Archive talks about archiving operations</div></div></div>\n<p>Created in early 2006, Archive-It<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> is a web archiving subscription service that allows institutions and individuals to build and preserve collections of digital content and create digital archives. Archive-It allows the user to customize their capture or exclusion of web content they want to preserve for cultural heritage reasons. Through a web application, Archive-It partners can harvest, catalog, manage, browse, search, and view their archived collections.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In terms of accessibility, the archived web sites are full text searchable within seven days of capture.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Content collected through Archive-It is captured and stored as a <a href="/wiki/Web_ARChive" title="Web ARChive">WARC file</a>. A primary and back-up copy is stored at the Internet Archive data centers. A copy of the WARC file can be given to subscribing partner institutions for geo-redundant preservation and storage purposes to their best practice standards.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Periodically, the data captured through Archive-It is indexed into the Internet Archive\'s general archive.\n</p><p>As of March&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Archive-It had more than 275 partner institutions in 46 U.S. states and 16 countries that have captured more than 7.4 billion URLs for more than 2,444 public collections. Archive-It partners are universities and college libraries, state archives, federal institutions, museums, law libraries, and cultural organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Literature_Organization" title="Electronic Literature Organization">Electronic Literature Organization</a>, North Carolina State Archives and Library, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_American_University_in_Cairo" title="The American University in Cairo">American University in Cairo</a>, Georgetown Law Library, and many others.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_Archive_Scholar">Internet Archive Scholar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Internet Archive Scholar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 2020 Internet Archive announced a new initiative to archive and preserve <a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">open access</a> academic journals, called the "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://scholar.archive.org/">Internet Archive Scholar</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Its fulltext search index includes over 25 million research articles and other scholarly documents preserved in the Internet Archive. The collection spans from digitized copies of eighteenth century journals through the latest Open Access conference proceedings and pre-prints crawled from the World Wide Web.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Book_collections">Book collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Book collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Text_collection">Text collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Text collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg/220px-Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg/330px-Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg/440px-Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scribe_Machine_Acquisition_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Internet Archive "Scribe" <a href="/wiki/Book_scanning" title="Book scanning">book scanning</a> workstation</div></div></div>\n<p>The Internet Archive operates 33 <a href="/wiki/Book_scanning" title="Book scanning">scanning centers</a> in five countries, digitizing about 1,000 books a day for a total of more than 2 million books,<sup id="cite_ref-Hoffelder2013_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffelder2013-71">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> financially supported by libraries and foundations.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;notes 29&#93;</a></sup> As of July&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the collection included 4.4 million books with more than 15 million downloads per month.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoffelder2013_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffelder2013-71">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> As of November&#160;2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, when there were approximately 1 million texts, the entire collection was greater than 0.5 petabytes, which includes raw camera images, cropped and skewed images, <a href="/wiki/PDF" title="PDF">PDFs</a>, and raw <a href="/wiki/Optical_character_recognition" title="Optical character recognition">OCR</a> data.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Between about 2006 and 2008, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> had a special relationship with Internet Archive texts through its <a href="/wiki/Live_Search_Books" title="Live Search Books">Live Search Books</a> project, scanning more than 300,000 books that were contributed to the collection, as well as financial support and scanning equipment. On May 23, 2008, Microsoft announced it would be ending the Live Book Search project and no longer scanning books.<sup id="cite_ref-msdown_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdown-74">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Microsoft made its scanned books available without contractual restriction and donated its scanning equipment to its former partners.<sup id="cite_ref-msdown_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdown-74">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg/220px-A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg/330px-A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg/440px-A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Real_Page-Turner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Internet Archive in-house scan ongoing</div></div></div>\n<p>Around October 2007, Archive users began uploading public domain books from <a href="/wiki/Google_Books" title="Google Books">Google Book Search</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;notes 30&#93;</a></sup> As of November&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were more than 900,000 Google-digitized books in the Archive\'s collection;<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;notes 31&#93;</a></sup> the books are identical to the copies found on Google, except without the Google watermarks, and are available for unrestricted use and download.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Brewster Kahle revealed in 2013 that this archival effort was coordinated by <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Swartz" title="Aaron Swartz">Aaron Swartz</a>, who with a "bunch of friends" downloaded the public domain books from Google slow enough and from enough computers to stay within Google\'s restrictions. They did this to ensure public access to the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>. The Archive ensured the items were attributed and linked back to Google, which never complained, while libraries "grumbled". According to Kahle, this is an example of Swartz\'s "genius" to work on what could give the most to the public good for millions of people.<sup id="cite_ref-kahle-aswmem_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kahle-aswmem-78">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <span class="anchor" id="RECAP_US_Federal_Court_Documents"></span>Besides books, the Archive offers free and anonymous public access to more than four million court opinions, legal briefs, or exhibits uploaded from the <a href="/wiki/Federal_judiciary_of_the_United_States" title="Federal judiciary of the United States">United States Federal Courts</a>\' <a href="/wiki/PACER_(law)" title="PACER (law)">PACER</a> electronic document system via the <a href="/wiki/RECAP" class="mw-redirect" title="RECAP">RECAP</a> web browser plugin. These documents had been kept behind a federal court paywall. On the Archive, they had been accessed by more than six million people by 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-kahle-aswmem_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kahle-aswmem-78">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Archive\'s BookReader <a href="/wiki/Web_app" class="mw-redirect" title="Web app">web app</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BookReader_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BookReader-79">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> built into its website, has features such as single-page, two-page, and <a href="/wiki/Thumbnail" title="Thumbnail">thumbnail</a> modes; fullscreen mode; <a href="/wiki/Page_zooming" title="Page zooming">page zooming</a> of <a href="/wiki/High-resolution" class="mw-redirect" title="High-resolution">high-resolution</a> images; and <a href="/wiki/Flip_page" title="Flip page">flip page</a> animation.<sup id="cite_ref-BookReader_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BookReader-79">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline"
