64&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Library">Open Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Open Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open_Library" title="Open Library">Open Library</a></div>\n<p>The Open Library is another project of the Internet Archive. The wiki seeks to include a web page for every book ever published: it holds 25 million catalog records of editions. It also seeks to be a web-accessible public library: it contains the full texts of approximately 1,600,000 public domain books (out of the more than five million from the main <a href="#Text_collection">texts collection</a>), as well as in-print and in-copyright books,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> many of which are fully readable, downloadable<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Full-text_search" title="Full-text search">full-text searchable</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> it offers a two-week loan of <a href="/wiki/E-book" class="mw-redirect" title="E-book">e-books</a> in its <a href="/wiki/Controlled_digital_lending" title="Controlled digital lending">controlled digital lending</a> program for over 647,784 books not in the public domain, in partnership with over 1,000 library partners from 6 countries<sup id="cite_ref-Hoffelder2013_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffelder2013-71">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> after a free registration on the web site. Open Library is a <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source software</a> project, with its source code freely available on <a href="/wiki/GitHub" title="GitHub">GitHub</a>.\n</p><p>The Open Library faces objections from some authors and the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Authors" title="Society of Authors">Society of Authors</a>, who hold that the project is distributing books without authorization and is thus in violation of copyright laws,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and four major publishers initiated a copyright infringement lawsuit against the Internet Archive in June 2020 to stop the Open Library project.<sup id="cite_ref-open_library_lawsuit_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open_library_lawsuit-121">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digitizing_sponsors_for_books">Digitizing sponsors for books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Digitizing sponsors for books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Many large institutional sponsors have helped the Internet Archive provide millions of scanned publications (text items).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Some sponsors that have digitized large quantities of texts include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Robarts_Library" title="Robarts Library">Robarts Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta_Libraries" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Alberta Libraries">University of Alberta Libraries</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ottawa" title="University of Ottawa">University of Ottawa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Library_Consortium" title="Boston Library Consortium">Boston Library Consortium</a> member libraries, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Library" title="Boston Public Library">Boston Public Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Theological_Seminary_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Princeton Theological Seminary Library">Princeton Theological Seminary Library</a>, and many others.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, the <a href="/wiki/MIT_Press" title="MIT Press">MIT Press</a> authorized the Internet Archive to digitize and lend books from the press\'s <a href="/wiki/Backlist" title="Backlist">backlist</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> with financial support from the <a href="/wiki/Arcadia_Fund" title="Arcadia Fund">Arcadia Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> A year later, the Internet Archive received further funding from the Arcadia Fund to invite some other university presses to partner with the Internet Archive to digitize books, a project called "Unlocking University Press Books".<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> has created numerous <a href="/wiki/Handle_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Handle system">handle system</a> identifiers that point to free digitized books in the Internet Archive.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The Internet Archive and Open Library are listed on the Library of Congress website as a source of e-books.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_collections">Media collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Media collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/220px-Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/330px-Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/440px-Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Media_reader_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Media reader</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg/220px-Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg/330px-Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg/440px-Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unrelated_Microfilm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Microfilms at the Internet Archive</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/220px-Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/330px-Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/440px-Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Videocassettes_and_VCRs_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Videocassette" class="mw-redirect" title="Videocassette">Videocassettes</a> at the Internet Archive</div></div></div>\n<p>In addition to web archives, the Internet Archive maintains extensive collections of digital media that are attested by the uploader to be in the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a> in the United States or licensed under a license that allows redistribution, such as <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> licenses. Media are organized into collections by media type (moving images, audio, text, etc.), and into sub-collections by various criteria. Each of the main collections includes a "Community" sub-collection (formerly named "Open Source") where general contributions by the public are stored.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audio_collection">Audio collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Audio collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Live_Music_Archive" title="Live Music Archive">Live Music Archive</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Great_78_Project" title="The Great 78 Project">The Great 78 Project</a></div>\n<p>The Audio Archive includes music, <a href="/wiki/Audiobook" title="Audiobook">audiobooks</a>, news broadcasts, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Radio" title="Golden Age of Radio">old time radio</a> shows, and a wide variety of other audio files. There are more than 200,000 free digital recordings in the collection. The subcollections include audio books and poetry, <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcasts</a>, non-English audio, and many others.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;notes 65&#93;</a></sup> The sound collections are curated by <a href="/wiki/B._George" title="B. George">B. George</a>, director of the <a href="/wiki/ARChive_of_Contemporary_Music" title="ARChive of Contemporary Music">ARChive of Contemporary Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WP_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-132">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Live Music Archive sub-collection includes more than 170,000 concert recordings from independent musicians, as well as more established artists and musical ensembles with permissive rules about recording their concerts, such as the <a href="/wiki/Grateful_Dead" title="Grateful Dead">Grateful Dead</a>, and more recently, <a href="/wiki/The_Smashing_Pumpkins" title="The Smashing Pumpkins">The Smashing Pumpkins</a>. Also, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Zevon" title="Jordan Zevon">Jordan Zevon</a> has allowed the Internet Archive to host a definitive collection of his father <a href="/wiki/Warren_Zevon" title="Warren Zevon">Warren Zevon</a>\'s concert recordings. The Zevon collection ranges from 1976 to 2001 and contains 126 concerts including 1,137 songs.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Great 78 Project aims to digitize 250,000 78 rpm singles (500,000 songs) from the period between 1880 and 1960, donated by various collectors and institutions. It has been developed in collaboration with the Archive of Contemporary Music and George Blood Audio, responsible for the audio digitization.<sup id="cite_ref-WP_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP-132">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brooklyn_Museum">Brooklyn Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Brooklyn Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This collection contains approximately 3,000 items from <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Museum" title="Brooklyn Museum">Brooklyn Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;notes 66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Images_collection">Images collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Images collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This collection contains more than 3.5 million items.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MusicBrainz#Cover_Art_Archive" title="MusicBrainz">Cover Art Archive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a> - Gallery Images, NASA Images, <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> <a href="/wiki/Flickr" title="Flickr">Flickr</a> Archive, and <a href="/wiki/Libre_Map_Project" title="Libre Map Project">USGS Maps</a> and are some sub-collections of Image collection.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_Art_Archive">Cover Art Archive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cover Art Archive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_(2020).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_%282020%29.svg/220px-Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_%282020%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="42" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_%282020%29.svg/330px-Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_%282020%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_%282020%29.svg/440px-Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_%282020%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="97" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cover_Art_Archive_Logo_with_text_(2020).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of Cover Art Archive</div></div></div>\n<p>The Cover Art Archive is a joint project between the Internet Archive and <a href="/wiki/MusicBrainz" title="MusicBrainz">MusicBrainz</a>, whose goal is to make cover art images on the Internet. As of April&#160;2021,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> this collection contains more than 1,400,000 items.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;notes 67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_images">Metropolitan Museum of Art images</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Museum of Art images">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The images of this collection are from the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a>. This collection contains more than 140,000 items.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;notes 68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Images">NASA Images</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: NASA Images">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The NASA Images archive was created through a Space Act Agreement between the Internet Archive and NASA to bring public access to NASA\'s image, video, and audio collections in a single, searchable resource. The IA NASA Images team worked closely with all of the NASA centers to keep adding to the ever-growing collection.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The nasaimages.org site launched in July 2008 and had more than 100,000 items online at the end of its hosting in 2012.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupy_Wall_Street_Flickr_archive">Occupy Wall Street Flickr archive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Occupy Wall Street Flickr archive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>This collection contains creative commons licensed photographs from Flickr related to the Occupy Wall Street movement. This collection contains more than 15,000 items.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;notes 69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="USGS_Maps">USGS Maps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: USGS Maps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>This collection contains more than 59,000 items from <a href="/wiki/Libre_Map_Project" title="Libre Map Project">Libre Map Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;notes 70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Machinima_archive">Machinima archive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Machinima archive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>One of the sub-collections of the Internet Archive\'s Video Archive is the Machinima Archive. This small section hosts many Machinima videos. Machinima is a digital artform in which <a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">computer games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Game_engine" title="Game engine">game engines</a>, or software engines are used in a sandbox-like mode to create motion pictures, recreate plays, or even publish presentations or keynotes. The archive collects a range of Machinima films from internet publishers such as <a href="/wiki/Rooster_Teeth" title="Rooster Teeth">Rooster Teeth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machinima,_Inc." title="Machinima, Inc.">Machinima.com</a> as well as independent producers. The sub-collection is a collaborative effort among the Internet Archive, the How They Got Game research project at Stanford University, the Academy of Machinima Arts and Sciences, and Machinima.com.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;notes 71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Mathematics_.E2.80.93_Hamid_Naderi_Yeganeh"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematics_\xe2\x80\x93_Hamid_Naderi_Yeganeh">Mathematics \xe2\x80\x93 Hamid Naderi Yeganeh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mathematics \xe2\x80\x93 Hamid Naderi Yeganeh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This collection contains mathematical images created by mathematical artist <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Naderi_Yeganeh" title="Hamid Naderi Yeganeh">Hamid Naderi Yeganeh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;notes 72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Microfilm_collection">Microfilm collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Microfilm collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This collection contains approximately 160,000 items from a variety of libraries including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago#Library_system" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago Libraries</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Illinois at Urbana\xe2\x80\x93Champaign">University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allen_County_Public_Library" title="Allen County Public Library">Allen County Public Library</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Technical_Information_Service" title="National Technical Information Service">National Technical Information Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;notes 73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;notes 74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moving_image_collection">Moving image collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Moving image collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Special:WhatLinksHere/Template:Internet_Archive_film" title="Special:WhatLinksHere/Template:Internet Archive film">Wikipedia list of films freely available on the Internet Archive</a></div>\n<p>The Internet Archive holds a collection of approximately 3,863 feature films.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;notes 75&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, the Internet Archive\'s Moving Image collection includes: <a href="/wiki/Newsreel" title="Newsreel">newsreels</a>, classic <a href="/wiki/Cartoon" title="Cartoon">cartoons</a>, pro- and anti-war <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a>, The Video Cellar Collection, Skip Elsheimer\'s "A.V. Geeks" collection, early television, and ephemeral material from <a href="/wiki/Prelinger_Archives" title="Prelinger Archives">Prelinger Archives</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, educational, and industrial films, as well as amateur and home movie collections.\n</p><p>Subcategories of this collection include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>IA\'s <a href="/wiki/Brickfilm" title="Brickfilm"><i>Brick Films</i></a> collection, which contains <a href="/wiki/Stop_motion" title="Stop motion">stop-motion</a> animation filmed with <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> bricks, some of which are "remakes" of feature films.</li>\n<li>IA\'s <i>Election 2004</i> collection, a non-partisan public resource for sharing video materials related to the <a href="/wiki/2004_United_States_presidential_election" title="2004 United States presidential election">2004 United States presidential election</a>.</li>\n<li>IA\'s <i>FedFlix</i> collection, Joint Venture NTIS-1832 between the National Technical Information Service and Public.Resource.Org that features "the best movies of the United States Government, from training films to history, from our national parks to the <a href="/wiki/National_Fire_Academy" title="National Fire Academy">U.S. Fire Academy</a> and the Postal Inspectors"<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;notes 76&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>IA\'s <i>Independent News</i> collection, which includes sub-collections such as the Internet Archive\'s World At War competition from 2001, in which contestants created short films demonstrating "why access to history matters". Among their most-downloaded video files are eyewitness recordings of the devastating <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake</a>.</li>\n<li>IA\'s <i>September 11 Television Archive</i>, which contains archival footage from the world\'s major television networks of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">terrorist attacks</a> of September 11, 2001, as they unfolded on live television.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;notes 77&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netlabels"><span id="Netlabels">Netlabels</span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Netlabels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Netlabel" title="Netlabel">Netlabel</a>.</div>\n<p>The Archive has a collection of freely distributable music that is streamed and available for download via its <i>Netlabels</i> service. The music in this collection generally has Creative Commons-license catalogs of virtual record labels.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;notes 78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lifehacker_free_music_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lifehacker_free_music-149">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Educational_Resources">Open Educational Resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Open Educational Resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Open Educational Resources</i> is a digital collection at archive.org. This collection contains hundreds of free courses, video lectures, and supplemental materials from universities in the United States and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. The contributors of this collection are <a href="/wiki/ArsDigita_University" title="ArsDigita University">ArsDigita University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Foundation" title="Hewlett Foundation">Hewlett Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlebury_Institute_of_International_Studies_at_Monterey" title="Middlebury Institute of International Studies at Monterey">Monterey Institute</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Naropa_University" title="Naropa University">Naropa University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;notes 79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="TV_News_Search_.26_Borrow"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="TV_News_Search_&amp;_Borrow">TV News Search &amp; Borrow</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: TV News Search &amp; Borrow">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg/220px-TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg/330px-TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg/440px-TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TV_tuners_at_the_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>TV tuners at the Internet Archive</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2012, the Internet Archive launched the TV News Search &amp; Borrow service for searching U.S. national news programs.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;notes 80&#93;</a></sup> The service is built on closed captioning transcripts and allows users to search and stream 30-second video clips. Upon launch, the service contained "350,000 news programs collected over 3 years from national U.S. networks and stations in San Francisco and Washington D.C."<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> According to Kahle, the service was inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_Television_News_Archive" title="Vanderbilt Television News Archive">Vanderbilt Television News Archive</a>, a similar library of televised network news programs.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to Vanderbilt, which limits access to streaming video to individuals associated with subscribing colleges and universities, the TV News Search &amp; Borrow allows open access to its streaming video clips. In 2013, the Archive received an additional donation of "approximately 40,000 well-organized tapes" from the estate of a <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> woman, <a href="/wiki/Marion_Stokes" title="Marion Stokes">Marion Stokes</a>. Stokes "had recorded more than 35 years of TV news in Philadelphia and <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> with her <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Betamax" title="Betamax">Betamax</a> machines."<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Michelson_library">Michelson library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Michelson library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In December 2020, the film research library of <a href="/wiki/Lillian_Michelson" title="Lillian Michelson">Lillian Michelson</a> was donated to the archive.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_services_and_endeavors">Other services and endeavors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Other services and endeavors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_media">Physical media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Physical media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/220px-Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/330px-Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/440px-Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vintage_wall_intercom_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A vintage wall intercom, an example of another "archived" item</div></div></div>\n<p>Voicing a strong reaction to the idea of books simply being thrown away, and inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Svalbard_Global_Seed_Vault" title="Svalbard Global Seed Vault">Svalbard Global Seed Vault</a>, Kahle now envisions collecting one copy of every book ever published. "We\'re not going to get there, but that\'s our goal", he said. Alongside the books, Kahle plans to store the Internet Archive\'s old servers, which were replaced in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software">Software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Internet Archive has "the largest collection of historical software online in the world", spanning 50 years of <a href="/wiki/History_of_computing_hardware" title="History of computing hardware">computer history</a> in <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Terabyte">terabytes</a> of computer magazines and journals, books, <a href="/wiki/Shareware" title="Shareware">shareware</a> discs, FTP sites, <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a>, etc. The Internet Archive has created an archive of what it describes as "vintage software", as a way to preserve them.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;notes 81&#93;</a></sup> The project advocated for an exemption from the United States <a href="/wiki/Digital_Millennium_Copyright_Act" title="Digital Millennium Copyright Act">Digital Millennium Copyright Act</a> to permit them to bypass <a href="/wiki/Copy_protection" title="Copy protection">copy protection</a>, which was approved in 2003 for a period of three years.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;notes 82&#93;</a></sup> The Archive does not offer the software for download, as the exemption is solely "for the purpose of preservation or archival reproduction of published digital works by a library or archive."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The exemption was renewed in 2006, and in 2009 was indefinitely extended pending further rulemakings.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The Library reiterated the exemption as a "Final Rule" with no expiration date in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-75_fr_43825_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75_fr_43825-161">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the Internet Archive began to provide <a href="/wiki/Abandonware" title="Abandonware">abandonware</a> video games <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">browser</a>-playable via <a href="/wiki/Multi_Emulator_Super_System" title="Multi Emulator Super System">MESS</a>, for instance the <a href="/wiki/Atari_2600" title="Atari 2600">Atari 2600</a> game <a href="/wiki/E.T._the_Extra-Terrestrial_(video_game)" title="E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial (video game)"><i>E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Since December 23, 2014, the Internet Archive presents, via a browser-based <a href="/wiki/DOSBox" title="DOSBox">DOSBox</a> emulation, thousands of <a href="/wiki/MS-DOS" title="MS-DOS">DOS</a>/PC games<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;notes 83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> for <i>"scholarship and research purposes only"</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;notes 84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In November 2020, the Archive introduced a new emulator for <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a> called <a href="/wiki/Ruffle_(software)" title="Ruffle (software)">Ruffle</a>, and began archiving Flash animations and games ahead of the December 31, 2020 end-of-life for the Flash plugin across all computer systems.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Table_Top_Scribe_System"><span class="anchor" id="ttscribe"></span>Table Top Scribe System</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Table Top Scribe System">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A combined hardware software system has been developed that performs a safe method of digitizing content.<sup id="cite_ref-ttscribe1_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ttscribe1-171">&#91;notes 85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LinuxsSavesCongress_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LinuxsSavesCongress-172">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Credit_Union">Credit Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Credit Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From 2012 to November 2015, the Internet Archive operated the Internet Archive Federal Credit Union, a <a href="/wiki/Federal_credit_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal credit union">federal credit union</a> based in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick, New Jersey</a>, with the goal of providing access to low- and middle-income people. Throughout its short existence, the IAFCU experienced significant conflicts with the <a href="/wiki/National_Credit_Union_Administration" title="National Credit Union Administration">National Credit Union Administration</a>, which severely limited the IAFCU\'s loan portfolio and concerns over serving <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">Bitcoin</a> firms. At the time of its dissolution, it consisted of 395 members and was worth $2.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies_and_legal_disputes">Controversies and legal disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Controversies and legal disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine#In_legal_evidence" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine \xc2\xa7&#160;In legal evidence</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_(2013).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_%282013%29.jpg/220px-The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_%282013%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_%282013%29.jpg/330px-The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_%282013%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_%282013%29.jpg/440px-The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_%282013%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_main_hall_at_Internet_Archive_(2013).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main hall of the current headquarters</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grateful_Dead">Grateful Dead</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Grateful Dead">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In November 2005, free downloads of <a href="/wiki/Grateful_Dead" title="Grateful Dead">Grateful Dead</a> concerts were removed from the site. <a href="/wiki/John_Perry_Barlow" title="John Perry Barlow">John Perry Barlow</a> identified <a href="/wiki/Bob_Weir" title="Bob Weir">Bob Weir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Hart" title="Mickey Hart">Mickey Hart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Kreutzmann" title="Bill Kreutzmann">Bill Kreutzmann</a> as the instigators of the change, according to an article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-leeds_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leeds-175">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phil_Lesh" title="Phil Lesh">Phil Lesh</a> commented on the change in a November 30, 2005, posting to his personal web site:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It was brought to my attention that all of the Grateful Dead shows were taken down from Archive.org right before <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving" title="Thanksgiving">Thanksgiving</a>. I was not part of this decision making process and was not notified that the shows were to be pulled. I do feel that the music is the Grateful Dead\'s legacy and I hope that one way or another all of it is available for those who want it.<sup id="cite_ref-lesh_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lesh-176">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>A November 30 forum post from <a href="/wiki/Brewster_Kahle" title="Brewster Kahle">Brewster Kahle</a> summarized what appeared to be the compromise reached among the band members. Audience recordings could be downloaded or streamed, but <a href="/wiki/Mixing_console" title="Mixing console">soundboard</a> recordings were to be available for streaming only. Concerts have since been re-added.<sup id="cite_ref-kahle_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kahle-177">&#91;notes 86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_security_letters">National security letters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: National security letters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="National_security_letter"></span>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/w/index.php?title=File:EFF-IA_National_security_letter.pdf&amp;page=2" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/EFF-IA_National_security_letter.pdf/page2-160px-EFF-IA_National_security_letter.pdf.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="207" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">A <a href="/wiki/National_security_letter" title="National security letter">national security letter</a> issued to the Internet Archive demanding information about a user</div></div></div></div>\n<p>On May 8, 2008, it was revealed that the Internet Archive had successfully challenged an <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> <a href="/wiki/National_security_letter" title="National security letter">national security letter</a> asking for logs on an undisclosed user.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 28, 2016, it was revealed that a second FBI national security letter had been successfully challenged that had been asking for logs on another undisclosed user.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_SOPA_and_PIPA_bills">Opposition to SOPA and PIPA bills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Opposition to SOPA and PIPA bills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Internet Archive blacked out its web site for 12 hours on January 18, 2012, in protest of the <a href="/wiki/Stop_Online_Piracy_Act" title="Stop Online Piracy Act">Stop Online Piracy Act</a> and the <a href="/wiki/PROTECT_IP_Act" title="PROTECT IP Act">PROTECT IP Act</a> <a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" title="Bill (law)">bills</a>, two pieces of legislation in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> that they claimed would "negatively affect the ecosystem of web publishing that led to the emergence of the Internet Archive". This occurred in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Protests_against_SOPA_and_PIPA#Wikimedia_community" title="Protests against SOPA and PIPA">English Wikipedia blackout</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Protests_against_SOPA_and_PIPA" title="Protests against SOPA and PIPA">numerous other protests</a> across the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_Google_Books_settlement">Opposition to Google Books settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Opposition to Google Books settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Internet Archive is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Open_Book_Alliance" title="Open Book Alliance">Open Book Alliance</a>, which has been among the most outspoken critics of the <a href="/wiki/Google_Book_Search_Settlement_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Book Search Settlement Agreement">Google Book Settlement</a>. The Archive advocates an alternative digital library project.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nintendo_Power_magazine"><i>Nintendo Power</i> magazine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Nintendo Power magazine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In February 2016, Internet Archive users had begun archiving digital copies of <i><a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Power" title="Nintendo Power">Nintendo Power</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>\'s official magazine for their games and products, which ran from 1988 to 2012. The first 140 issues had been collected, before Nintendo had the archive removed on August 8, 2016. In response to the take-down, Nintendo told gaming website <i><a href="/wiki/Polygon_(website)" title="Polygon (website)">Polygon</a></i>, "[Nintendo] must protect our own characters, trademarks and other content. The unapproved use of Nintendo\'s intellectual property can weaken our ability to protect and preserve it, or to possibly use it for new projects".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_of_India">Government of India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Government of India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In August 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Telecommunications" title="Department of Telecommunications">Department of Telecommunications</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> blocked the Internet Archive along with other file-sharing websites, in accordance with two court orders issued by the <a href="/wiki/Madras_High_Court" title="Madras High Court">Madras High Court</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gtech_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gtech-184">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> citing piracy concerns after copies of two <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> films were allegedly shared via the service.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">HTTP</a> version of the Archive was blocked but it remained accessible using the <a href="/wiki/HTTPS" title="HTTPS">HTTPS</a> protocol.<sup id="cite_ref-gtech_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gtech-184">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_Turkey" title="Censorship in Turkey">Censorship in Turkey</a></div>\n<p>On October 9, 2016, the Internet Archive was temporarily blocked in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> after it was used (amongst other file hosters) by hackers to host 17 GB of leaked government emails.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Emergency_Library">National Emergency Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: National Emergency Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the midst of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> which closed many schools, universities, and libraries, the Archive announced on March 24, 2020 that it was creating the National Emergency Library by removing the lending restrictions it had in place for 1.4 million digitized books in its Open Library but otherwise limiting users to the number of books they could check out and enforcing their return; normally, the site would only allow one digital lending for each physical copy of the book they had, by use of an <a href="/wiki/Encryption" title="Encryption">encrypted file</a> that would become unusable after the lending period was completed. This Library would remain as such until at least June 30, 2020 or until the US national emergency was over, whichever came later.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> At launch, the Internet Archive allowed authors and rightholders to submit opt-out requests for their works to be omitted from the National Emergency Library.<sup id="cite_ref-ArchiveResponse_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArchiveResponse-189">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Internet Archive said the National Emergency Library addressed an "unprecedented global and immediate need for access to reading and research material" due to the closures of physical libraries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> They justified the move in a number of ways. Legally, they said they were promoting access to those inaccessible resources, which they claimed was an exercise in Fair Use principles. The Archive continued implementing their <a href="/wiki/Controlled_digital_lending" title="Controlled digital lending">controlled digital lending</a> policy that predated the National Emergency Library, meaning they still encrypted the lent copies and it was no easier for users to create new copies of the books than before. An ultimate determination of whether or not the National Emergency Library constituted Fair Use could only be made by a court. Morally, they also pointed out that the Internet Archive was a registered library like any other, that they either paid for the books themselves or received them as donations, and that lending through libraries predated copyright restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-ArchiveResponse_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArchiveResponse-189">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, the Archive had already been criticized by authors and publishers for its prior lending approach, and upon announcement of the National Emergency Library, authors, publishers, and groups representing both took further issue, equating the move to <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a> and digital piracy, and using the COVID-19 pandemic as a reason to push the boundaries of copyright (see also: <a href="/wiki/Open_Library#Copyright_violation_accusations" title="Open Library">Open Library \xc2\xa7&#160;Copyright violation accusations</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> After the works of some of these authors were ridiculed in responses, the Internet Archive\'s <a href="/wiki/Jason_Scott" title="Jason Scott">Jason Scott</a> requested that supporters of the National Emergency Library not denigrate anyone\'s books: "I realize there\'s strong debate and disagreement here, but books are life-giving and life-changing and these writers made them."<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Publishers.27_lawsuit"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishers\'_lawsuit">Publishers\' lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Publishers&#039; lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The operation of the National Emergency Library is part of a lawsuit filed against the Internet Archive by four major book publishers in June 2020, challenging the copyright validity of the controlled digital lending program.<sup id="cite_ref-open_library_lawsuit_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open_library_lawsuit-121">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In response, the Internet Archive closed the National Emergency Library on June 16, 2020, rather than the planned June 30, 2020, due to the lawsuit.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The plaintiffs, supported by the <a href="/wiki/Copyright_Alliance" title="Copyright Alliance">Copyright Alliance</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> claimed in their lawsuit that the Internet Archive\'s actions constituted a "willful mass copyright infringement". Additionally, Senator <a href="/wiki/Thom_Tillis" title="Thom Tillis">Thom Tillis</a> (R-North Carolina), chairman of the intellectual property subcommittee on the Senate Judiciary Committee, said in a letter to the Internet Archive that he was "concerned that the Internet Archive thinks that it \xe2\x80\x93 not Congress \xe2\x80\x93 gets to determine the scope of copyright law".<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In August 2020 the lawsuit trial was tentatively scheduled to begin in November 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As part of its response to the publishers\' lawsuit, in late 2020 the Archive launched a campaign called Empowering Libraries (hashtag #EmpoweringLibraries) that portrayed the lawsuit as a threat to all libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2020, <i><a href="/wiki/Publishers_Weekly" title="Publishers Weekly">Publishers Weekly</a></i> included the lawsuit among its "Top 10 Library Stories of 2020".<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceramic_archivists_collection">Ceramic archivists collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Ceramic archivists collection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/220px-Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/330px-Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg/440px-Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceramic_Archivists_by_sculptor_Nuala_Creed_at_Internet_Archive.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">Ceramic</a> figures of Internet Archive employees</div></div></div>\n<p>The Great Room of the Internet Archive features a collection of more than 100 <a href="/wiki/Ceramic_art" title="Ceramic art">ceramic figures</a> representing employees of the Internet Archive. This collection, inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Terracotta_Army" title="Terracotta Army">statues of the Xian warriors in China</a>, was commissioned by Brewster Kahle, sculpted by <a href="/wiki/Nuala_Creed" title="Nuala Creed">Nuala Creed</a>, and is ongoing.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artists_in_residence">Artists in residence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Internet_Archive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Artists in residence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Internet Archive visual arts residency,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> organized by Amir Saber Esfahani, is designed to connect emerging and mid-career artists with the Archive\'s millions of collections and to show what is possible when open <a href="/wiki/Access_to_information" class="mw-redirect" title="Access to information">access to information</a> intersects with the arts. During this one-year residency, selected artists develop a body of work that responds to and utilizes the Archive\'s collections in their own practice.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>2019 Residency Artists: <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Duarte" title="Caleb Duarte">Caleb Duarte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Lynn" title="Whitney Lynn">Whitney Lynn</a>, and Jeffrey Alan Scudder.\n</p><p>2018 Residency Artists: Mieke Marple, Chris Sollars, and <a href="/wiki/Taravat_Talepasand" title="Taravat Talepasand">Taravat Talepasand</a>.\n</p><p>2017 Residency Artists: Laura Kim, Jeremiah Jenkins, and Jenny Odell\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span The archive provides a link to Google for PDF copies, but also maintains a local PDF copy, which is viewable under the "All Files: HTTPS" link.
